text:
I've been using this recipe (with a slight variation) for many years.  Instead of frying, I bake it in the oven.  Melting the butter and adding it to the breadcrumbs BEFORE you bread the chicken helps make the coating crispy in the oven.  I also vary the spices depending on what I'm serving...sometimes more thyme, basil, oregano, garlic.  Bake for 30 minutes or so, at 375.  Always very good, tender, and juicy.  Also makes good chicken strips and nuggets.

text:
This is pretty good, however, the chicken is sort of bland.  Needs some dressing up with seasoning.  I pan fried about 2 pieces of chicken first and tasted them.  My daughter and I agreed that it was indeed lacking something.  So on the next few pieces, I seasoned the chicken with some lemon pepper and extra basil, then added some garlic powder.  I should have added garlic salt, but didn't have any.  It still needed something. The crust is very good and crispy.  I like the recipe and will use it again, but I need to find a seasoning combination that will enhance the flavor of the chicken.  Maybe I will omit the butter and use extra virgin olive oil and add some garlic to it.  Thanks, though.

Very good and very simple recipe.  The only thing I did different was that I added 2 cloves of finely chopped garlic to the egg mixture and I dipped the chicken in the egg mix then the bread crumbs, then dipped the same piece of chicken into the egg mix again and then the breadcrumbs again so it gave it a thicker crust.  Great recipe!!!

My mother made this for us when I was little.  It was one of the only thing all of us (there are five) would eat.  You can do just about anything with it.  Definately use italian bread crumbs.  Sometimes we would make sandwiches and top with mayo, lettuce and tomato.  I have also cut the chicken into strips and made "chicken fingers".  My favorite though is to add marinara sauce to the pan (drain any excess oil) and top with mozzarella and parmasean.

text:
This recipe is superb and really easy. I took the advice from BUZZYSMOM and added butter to the bread crumb mix and I also added a bit of olive oil and garlic powder and I used a wisk ( I would recommend a wisk and not a fork- the wisk worked better) to mix everything up.  I poured a minimal layer of Prego Spaghetti sauce (meat flavored because it's all I had) on the bottom of the glass baking dish and then placed the battered chicken on top of the sauce. I baked the chicken in the oven for 35 minutes at 375 and then pulled out the dish...sprinkled shredded parmesan cheese and shredded cheddar cheese on the top of the chicken and then put it back in the oven for 3 minutes to melt the cheese a bit. EVERYONE in my family (including my culinary grad Sister and picky 82 year old Grandmother!) LOVED IT! I served this chicken parmesan with spaghetti and french bread- THANKS for this recipe and the helpful reviews and alterations everyone made to it!

text:
I made this the first according to the recipe and everyone thought it was too bland.  The next time I made it I added 1/2 teaspooon sage, 1/2 teaspoon italian seasoning, and 1/2 teaspoon paprika.  I also melted the butter and added it to the bread crumb mixture and 1/2 cup parmesan cheese instead of the 1/4 cup.  I baked it in the oven for about 30 minutes in a 350 degrees oven.  When there was 5 minutes left on the timer I took them out and flipped them.  My family liked this way so much better we are having it again tonight for dinner.

text:
Easy and delicious! I did make one change and that is...I didn't fry it!  Instead, I baked it at 400 degrees for 20 minutes (as per the Shake n Bake box instructions for boneless chicken)...no flattening, no mess, no extra pans, its healthier, less work and best of all, I don't have to worry about the chicken not cooking properly!  Unless it's completely submerged in oil (aka deep frying) I always bake my chicken for safety reasons. Also, the oven will cook your chicken to perfection, so there will be no risk of burning and your chicken will look beautiful everytime! For that golden brown look, drizzle melted spread over the chicken before putting it in the oven. I use Italian bread crumbs and it works perfectly.  This is even more delicious over pasta and topped with melted cheese. Yum!

I have taken advice of others and I add 1/4 tsp of garlic powder, thyme and oregano, 1 tsp basil and 1/4 tsp salt to the Italian seasoned bread crumbs. text:
This recipe is amazing! Seriously the best and easiest parmesan chicken I've ever made.  And super tasty! I changed a few things though.

First, I didn't have chicken breast so I used 6 chicken tenders instead.  I used fresh basil (approx. 1 TB) and added fresh thyme (approx. 1tsp).  I also used extra virgin olive oil instead of vegetable oil and dipped in the egg and EVOO, no butter.  After dredging through bread crumb mixture I laid them in a baking pan and sprinkled the remaining crumbs over chicken and thinly sliced 1 TB cold butter and laid this over chicken.  Then baked at 375* uncovered for about 30 minutes.  This was so tender and juicy I couldn't believe it! The butter on top gave it a nice crispy coating and wonderful flavor. 

I will be making this again many times I'm sure! My husband and 2 boys loved it!

My 6 year old adored this recipe and asked to add it to next week's menu.  That's rare from my picky little guy!  I did change the recipe a little bit.  I upped the parmesan to about 1/3 c.  I also added Italian seasoning, garlic powder & onion flakes.  I dipped the chicken in the egg, in the crumbs, back in the egg, and back in the crumbs for a thicker crust.  I cooked it on a cooling rack on a cookie sheet at 375 for 40 minutes.  Came out perfect.  I will make it again, but I will probably play with the spices a little more.

text:
My husband approved of this recipe!  Like a few other reviewers, I added butter to the Italian bread crumb mixture before coating the chicken, then put the chicken in a glass baking dish lightly coated with EVOO and marinara sauce with a few tablespoons of chopped garlic.  I baked it at 375 for 30 minutes.  In the last five minutes of baking, I melted mozzarella cheese on top of the chicken breasts.  To serve, I put the chicken breasts on top of spaghetti and covered everything with another layer of marinara.  The chicken was moist and flavorful, though I think marinating it in something like Italian dressing for a few hours before coating it with bread crumbs would add an additional layer of flavor to the meat.

I have been making this for many years. My grandmother was Sicilian and had a slightly different version of this recipe. I have changed it somewhat. I use half breadcrumbs half Italian seasoned panko crumbs, the Parmesan cheese, and I fry the pieces in olive oil. If you want make a lemon butter sauce and serve along with the chicken. This recipe works well using very thin slices of sandwich steak. pound the the beef as you would the chicken everything else is the same. It's one of my family favorites.

This was very good. Pretty much followed directions except I baked at 425 for about 25 minutes as I didn't feel like taking the time to flatten the chicken. My cooktop was not working so I didn't brown the chicken on the stove either. When the chicken was almost done, I put some garlic bread in the oven, then sliced the chicken & melted provolone cheese on top. When garlic bread was done, I put chicken/cheese on the top to serve as open faced sandwiches with marinara sauce over the chicken & garlic bread. Yummy!

region:

country:
None
text:
This is easily the best chicken parm I have made.  I did make the following adjustments:  I used chicken tenders rather than breasts.  I pounded them to tenderize and pulled out that white strip they always have (what is that?) which nicely sectioned off some chicken nuggets for my two year old.  I didn't have seasoned bread crumbs so I put some whole grain saltines in the food processor along with parmigiano reggiano and some "pasta sprinkle" from Penzey's Spices.  It's a blend of sweet basil, turkish oregano, thyme and garlic.  I processed everything together until it was a light crumb consistency.  I used the egg and crumb coating as described.  Rather than pan frying, I put the chicken strips on a non-stick cookie sheet.  Following a previous reviewer's advice, I lightly brushed the chicken with melted butter before baking at 425 degrees for about 30 mins.  I did flip the chicken about 20 minutes in.  It browned perfectly and came out with a crispy coating I've never gotten out of an oven baked chicken.  I served it with the Tomato Basil Penne Pasta submitted by timbertiger on this site.  I noted my changes to that recipe in the reviews.  FANTASTIC meal!

text:
Fast and simple to 'throw together' for a restaurant style meal.  I recommend using a tenderizer or meat pounder (other side of the tenderizer, forget proper name) and make sure the chicken is the thickness the recipe calls for (otherwise it doesn't cook through) and ALWAYS put make sure the pan with oil/butter is HOT before the meat goes in, otherwise chef Gordon Ramsey (Hell's Kitchen) says it will absorb the oil and affect taste. Ha Ha.  Great dish, looks pleasing if you make a side of spaghetti, this dish should be topped with a red sauce or alfredo.

text:
Delicious! I've made this dish before using another recipe, but I took the suggestions of other reviewers and it turned out great! I flattened the chicken to approx. 1/4" in a plastic baggie using a meat tenderizer tool. Then used the olive oil/garlic salt instead of egg and used plain breadcrumbs (less sodium) and added in basil, parmesan cheese, oregano, parsley, and garlic powder. Sprinkled shredded mozz. cheese (covering it with foil for half of cooking time to avoid burning cheese ~ 30 mins. at 375 degrees F)and served over spaghetti and additional tomato sauce. Yum! Will be making this again!

This was delicious!  I added some garlic and onion powder to the breading mixture, and some chopped garlic to the butter/oil.  I think it really helps enhance the flavors.  Also, after the chicken was finished in the pan, I topped with a bit of mozzarella cheese and broiled in the oven for 2-3 minutes.  The cheese comes out perfectly bubbly, and it doesn't over-cook the chicken!  I served over spaghetti and marinara sauce.  We will definitely be having this again.

text:
Very easy to make and was thoroughly enjoyed by everyone!
I only had boneless chicken thighs so cut them up and pounded those instead, was still juicy and yummy. I decided to use garlic salt instead of plain salt, and mixed herbs, lots of flavour this way. I looove parmesan and sneaked a bit extra into the mixture! Then instead of butter, I fried them in ghee as it doesnt burn. I also let them sit for a bit in the fridge then on the side before frying which i think helps the batter mix stay on the chicken better while cooking! 
Served with little herbed roast potato cubes n green beans with a little garlic butter. 
All plates were cleared and extras eaten as seconds!

text:
I really like this recipe, mainly because of its simplicity and how easy it was to cook.  Everything came out great, however I thought it was somewhat bland.  Here is what I added to the basic recipe: 1/2 tsp ea. of salt, pepper, oregano, garlic powder, italian seasoning, & cayenne pepper. Also I recommend using two eggs instead of one.
These additions add much more flavor overall without taking away from the core recipe.  Of course, there are still many variations - salt vs. garlic salt, pepper vs. ground/cracked pepper, etc.  Essentially you can make this as spicy or tasty as you'd like, but even if you use the original recipe you will be pleased with the result.

This recipe was easy and delicious! The only things I did differently were: I used fresh, shredded parmesan cheese (instead of grated in a can) and I baked mine in the oven, for 45 minutes on 375.  I did NOT flatten the chicken, so if you flatten it, you probably only need to bake it about 30-35 minutes.  I covered it with foil for the second half of cooking time, because the cheese was getting too dark.  My husband and 2 year old son also loved it!  Thanks for a great recipe!!  :)

My family loved this chicken!  It was a little bland so I did make some changes to it though.  I did flatten chicken to 1/4 inch thickness (That is important) and used the recipe ingredients except for the veg. oil.  I added a more basil to measure 3/4 tsp. and I added 1/2 tsp more oregeno, increased GRATED permesan cheese to almost 1/2 cup (Use the grated for the correct texture) a little garlic and I baked it at 375 for about 35 minutes instead of pan frying using a little olive oil in the bottom of the baking dish and turning so not to stick to dish. Just a few minutes before done I sprinkled some shredded mozz. cheese on top and served over a nest of pasta. Yummy.

text:
THIS IS A VERY EASY DISH TO PREPARE AND WAS EXTREMELY TASTY! I ESPECIALLY LIKE IT B/C THE INGREDIENTS CALLED FOR ARE ALL INGREDIENTS I KEEP ON-HAND, WHICH MAKES IT VERY SIMPLE. I ADDED SOME GARLIC SALT, DRIED ROSEMARY, THYME, (EXTRA) BASIL, OREGANO TO THE BREAD CRUMB MIXTURE. IT GAVE IT GREAT FLAVOR. I BEAT THE CHICKEN UNTIL IT WAS EVENLY FLAT (SOMEWHERE BETWEEN 1/4-1/2 INCH) AND COOKED IT IN THE SKILLET WITH OLIVE OIL (INSTEAD OF VEGETABLE OIL) AND FRESHLY MINCED GARLIC. IT COOKED QUICKLY (5 MIN PER SIDE) AND WAS VERY JUICY. I SERVED WITH A SIDE OF ANGEL HAIR PASTA & MARINARA SAUCE. IT WAS A HUGE HIT. LOVED IT! EVEN MY 1 1/2 YR OLD ENJOYED THE CHICKEN.
